		gads.src = (useSSL ? 'https:' : 'http:') + 
		'//www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js';
		var node = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0];
		node.parentNode.insertBefore(gads, node);
		})();
	</script>

<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">A broadband circularly polarized patch antenna is proposed for universal ultra-high-frequency (UHF) RF identification (RFID) applications. The antenna is composed of two corner-truncated patches and a suspended microstrip line with open-circuited termination. The main patch is fed by four probes which are sequentially connected to the suspended microstrip feed line. The measurement shows that the antenna achieves a return loss of -15 dB, gain of 8.3 dBic, axial ratio (AR) of 3 dB, and 3-dB AR beamwidth of 75<sup>deg</sup> over the UHF band of 818-964 MHz or 16.4%. Therefore, the proposed antenna is universal for UHF RFID applications worldwide at the UHF band of 840-960 MHz. In addition, a parametric study is conducted to facilitate the design and optimization processes for engineers.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>RF IDENTIFICATION (RFID), which was developed around World War II, is a technology that provides wireless identification and tracking capability. In recent years, RFID technology has been rapidly developed and applied to many service industries, distribution logistics, manufacturing companies, and goods flow systems <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>.</p><p>In an ultra-high-frequency (UHF) RFID system, the reader emits signals through reader antennas. When an RFID tag comprising an antenna and an application-specific integrated circuit (ASIC) is located in the reading zone of the reader antenna, the tag is activated and interrogated for its content information by the reader. The querying signal from the reader must have enough power to activate the tag ASIC to perform data processing, and transmit back a modulated string over a required reading distance. Since the RFID tags are always arbitrarily oriented in practical usage and the tag antennas are normally linearly polarized, circularly polarized (CP) reader antennas have been used in UHF RFID systems for ensuring the reliability of communications between readers and tags <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>.</p><p>Globally, each country has its own frequency allocation for UHF RFID applications, e.g., 840.5–844.5 and 920.5–924.5 MHz in China, 866–869 MHz in Europe, 902–928-MHz band in North and South of America, 866–869 and 920–925 MHz in Singapore, and 952–955 MHz in Japan, and so on, so that the UHF RFID frequency ranges from 840.5 to 955 MHz (a fractional bandwidth of 12.75%) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. Therefore, a universal reader antenna with desired performance across the entire UHF RFID band would be beneficial for RFID system configuration and implementation, as well as cost reduction.</p><p>In this paper, we propose a sequentially fed stacked CP patch antenna for UHF RFID applications. The antenna comprises two suspended truncated patches and a suspended microstrip line. The main patch is sequentially fed by four probes which are connected to the microstrip line. A parasitic patch is positioned right above the main patch for enhancing the bandwidth. The corners of the patches are truncated to enhance the axial ratio (AR) performance. The proposed antenna is designed to cover the UHF RFID band of 840–960 MHz with acceptable performance in terms of gain, AR, and impedance matching. Meanwhile, the antenna configuration is simple and easy for fabrication.</p><p>The remainder of this paper is organized as follows. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a> describes the geometry of the proposed antenna. The measured results, analysis, and discussion are presented in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a> demonstrates the results of parametric study. The validation of the proposed antenna in RFID system applications is exhibited in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a>. Finally, a conclusion is drawn in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec6" class="fulltext-link">Section VI</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna Configuration</h2></div><p>CP antennas can be realized when two orthogonal modes of equal amplitude are excited with a 90° phase difference <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2">[6]</a>. In general, the feeding structures of CP antennas can be categorized into single and hybrid feeds. A single feed of a CP antenna has the advantages of simple structure, easy manufacture, and small size in arrays. However, the single-fed single-patch CP antenna in its simple form has inherently narrow AR and impedance bandwidths of 1%–2% <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2">[7]</a>. To improve the bandwidth, a variety of CP antennas have been studied, wherein the bandwidth of AR, impedance matching, and gain have been enhanced, e.g., by modifying the radiator shape, designing feeding structures, and optimizing antenna or array configurations <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2">[8]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2">[9]</a>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2">[11]</a>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2">[12]</a>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2">[15]</a>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_2">[16]</a>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_2">[17]</a>. Usually, a CP antenna with the hybrid feed features a wide AR bandwidth, but suffers a complicated structure, expansive manufacture, and increased antenna size.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a> shows the configuration of the proposed antenna. The antenna comprises four layers of conductor, which include two suspended radiating patches, a suspended microstrip feed line, and a finite-size ground plane. Air substrate is used in this configuration to achieve higher gain, broader bandwidth, and lower cost. The microstrip feed line of a width of 24 mm is suspended above the ground plane (250 mm × 250 mm) at a height of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">h_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (5 mm). One end of the feed line is connected to an RF input, while the other one is open circuited, which simplifies the antenna structure. The main radiating patch of 156 mm × 156 mm and with a truncation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-8" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of 24.5 mm at two diagonal corners is placed above the feed line at spacing of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-16" role="math" style="width: 5.949em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.348em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.35em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-17"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-18"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-19" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-20"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-21"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-22" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-23" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-24" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">20</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-27"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-28"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-29"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-30" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">h_{2}=20\ {\hbox{mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The main patch is fed by four probes which are connected to the microstrip line. The probes are of diameter of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-31" role="math" style="width: 5.709em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.108em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.11em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-32"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-33" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-34" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2.2</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-36" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-37"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-38"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-39"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-40"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-41" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">d=2.2\ {\hbox{mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and positioned along the microstrip feed line with adequate distance to create the 90° phase lag between the probes and brings into sequential rotation of current on the radiation patch for CP radiation. To enhance the bandwidth, a truncated parasitic patch with a dimension of 139 mm × 139 mm and the truncation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-42" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-44" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-45"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-46" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-47"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-48"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-49" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">\Delta L_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of 17 mm is placed right above the main patch with the spacing of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-50" role="math" style="width: 5.949em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.348em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.35em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-51"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-52"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-53" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-54"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-55"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-56" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-57" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-58" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">10</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-59" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-60"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-61"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-62"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-63"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-64" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">h_{3}=10\ {\hbox{mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The truncated patches produce additional degenerating modes necessary for widening the AR bandwidth.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Configuration of the proposed antenna. (a) Exploded view. (b) Side view.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>With aid of simulation by Zeland IE3D, which is based on the method of moments (MoM), the antenna is optimized and then prototyped <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_2">[18]</a>. The prototype and detailed dimensions are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. The truncated patches, feed line, and ground plane are all made of copper and fixed using plastic spacers. Four metallic screws are used as the probes to connect the microstrip feed line and the main patch. A coaxial cable is directly connected to the microstrip feed line to simplify the assembly of the antenna, where the coaxial cable is split into two wires (screen and core) and the wires are soldered to the suspended feed line and the ground plane separately.

padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-118" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">250</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-119" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-120"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-121"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-122"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-123"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-124" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.413em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.421em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">L_{\rm g}=250\ {\hbox{mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). (a) Photograph of the antenna prototype. (b) Main patch. (c) Parasitic patch. (d) Microstrip feed line.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Results and Discussion</h2></div><p>The antenna was measured in an anechoic chamber using the Orbit MiDAS far-field measurement system and Agilent 8510C vector network analyzer.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> shows the simulated and measured return loss of the antenna. The measured return loss is less than −15 dB over the frequency range of 760–963 MHz (25.6%). <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a> exhibits the simulated and measured AR at boresight. The measured 3-dB AR bandwidth of 818–964 MHz or 16.4% is obtained. The simulated and measured boresight gain is illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(c)</a>. The antenna exhibits the measured gain of more than 8.3 dBic over the band of 815–970 MHz with a peak gain of 9.3 dBic at 900 MHz. The measured and simulated return loss, AR, and gain show good agreement.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Simulated and measured results of the proposed antenna. (a) Return loss. (b) AR. (c) Gain.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 4</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">5</a> show the measured radiation patterns at 840, 910, and 955 MHz in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-125" role="math" style="width: 2.526em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.285em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1002.28em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-126"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-127" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-129" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">x-z</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-130" role="math" style="width: 2.465em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.225em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1002.23em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-131"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-132" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-133" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-134" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">y-z</script></tex-math></inline-formula> planes, respectively. In both planes, symmetrical patterns and wide-angle AR characteristics have been observed. The beamwidth of 3-dB AR is more than 75°, which is desirable for wide-coverage RFID applications. The wider 3-dB AR beamwidth is accredited to the sequential feed arrangement. The advantage stems from the symmetry of the feeding structure, which cancelled out the unwanted cross polarization radiation. The 3-dB AR beamwidth of the antenna prototype at selected frequencies are tabulated in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Measured radiation patterns in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-135" role="math" style="width: 2.583em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.054em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.591em 1002.05em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-136"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-137" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-138" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.202em;">−</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-139" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.202em;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.754em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">x-z</script></tex-math></inline-formula> plane at: (a) 840, (b) 910, and (c) 955 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Measured radiation patterns in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-140" role="math" style="width: 2.517em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.987em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.591em 1001.99em 2.649em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-141"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-143" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.202em;">−</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-144" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.202em;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">y-z</script></tex-math></inline-formula> plane at: (a) 840, (b) 910, and (c) 955 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<p></p><p>In addition, the front-to-back ratio of the antenna is better than 15 dB in both the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-145" role="math" style="width: 2.526em; <div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Parametric Studies</h2></div><p>Parametric studies are conducted to provide more detailed information about the antenna design and optimization. The parametric study is carried out by simulation because good agreement between the simulation and measurement has been observed. The parameters under study include the truncation of the patches, the height of the parasitic patch, the size of feeding probes, the extension of the open-circuited microstrip line end, and the size of the ground plane. Since the effects of some parameters, such as the size and height of the main patch and the size of the parasitic patch, have been well known, the study of these parameters is excluded in this paper. To better understand the influence of the parameters on the performance of the antenna, only one parameter at a time will be varied, while others are kept unchanged unless especially indicated.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Truncation of the Main Patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-155" role="math" style="width: 2.185em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 112%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1001.91em 2.497em -999.98em); top: -2.18em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-156"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-157" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-158"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.094em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.172em 1000.66em 4.159em -999.98em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-159" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.842em; left: 0.678em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-160"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-161"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-162" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.185em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.23em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.109em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows the effect of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-163" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-164"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-165" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-166"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-167" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-168"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-169"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-170" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> on the return loss and AR of the antenna. It is found that the truncation of the main patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-171" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-172"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-173" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-174"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-175" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-176"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-177"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-178" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> shows a significant effect on the AR of the antenna. The nontruncated patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-179" role="math" style="width: 7.21em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.489em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.37em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-180"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-181" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-182" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-183"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-184" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-185"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-186"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-187" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-188" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-189" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-190" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-191"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-192"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-193"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-194"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-195" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-196" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">(\Delta L_{1}=0\ {\hbox{mm}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> exhibits the widest impedance bandwidth, but the narrowest AR bandwidth. The increasing of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-197" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-198"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-199" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-200"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-201" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-202"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-203"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-204" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> improves the AR bandwidth and achieves better impedance matching. However, over truncating (such as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-205" role="math" style="width: 6.91em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.189em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.19em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-206"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-207" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-208"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-209" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-210"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-211"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-212" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-213" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-214" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">55</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-215" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-216"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-217"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-218"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-219"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-220" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">\Delta L_{1}=55\ {\hbox{mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the patch will degrade all the bandwidths. The gain of the antenna is hardly affected by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-221" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-222"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-223" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-224"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-225" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-226"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-227"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-228" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> so that the results are not exhibited. In practical design, the truncation can be optimized for specific design requirement.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Effect of the truncation of the main patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-229" role="math" style="width: 2.45em; (a) Return loss. (b) AR.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Truncation of the Parasitic Patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-237" role="math" style="width: 2.185em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 112%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1001.91em 2.497em -999.98em); top: -2.18em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-238"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-239" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-240"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.094em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.172em 1000.66em 4.159em -999.98em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-241" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.842em; left: 0.678em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-242"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-243"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-244" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.185em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.23em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.109em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">\Delta L_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h3><p>Similar to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-245" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-246"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-247" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-248"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-249" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-250"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-251"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-252" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-253" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-254"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-255" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-256"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-257" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-258"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-259"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-260" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">\Delta L_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> has a greater effect on the AR and impedance bandwidths, while the gain of the antenna is hardly affected. As illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>, when the parasitic patch becomes a square <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-261" role="math" style="width: 7.21em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.489em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.37em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-262"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-263" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-264" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-265"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-266" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-267"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-268"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-269" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-270" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-271" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-272" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-273"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-274"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-275"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-276"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-277" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-278" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">(\Delta L_{2}=0\ {\hbox{mm}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the antenna features dramatic AR bandwidth reduction. The impedance and AR bandwidths change modestly if <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-279" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-280"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-281" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-282"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-283" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-284"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-285"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-286" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">\Delta L_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are kept within 10–20 mm and decline when the patch is over truncated.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Effect of the truncation of the parasitic patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-287" role="math" style="width: 2.45em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.921em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001.92em 2.583em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-288"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-289" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-290"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.665em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-292"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-293"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-294" style="font-size: 70.7%; (a) Return loss. (b) AR.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4c"><h3>C. Height of the Parasitic Patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-295" role="math" style="width: 1.146em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.99em; height: 0px; font-size: 112%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1000.97em 2.445em -999.98em); top: -2.128em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-296"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-297"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.99em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.172em 1000.56em 4.159em -999.98em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-298" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.842em; left: 0.574em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-299"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-300"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-301" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.133em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.23em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.109em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">h_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> exhibits the effect of varying height <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-302" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-303"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-304"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-305" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-306"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-307"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-308" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">h_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the parasitic patch on the performance of the antenna. It is observed that the operating band is shifted down as the height increases. Furthermore, the effect is more severe at higher frequencies. When the parasitic patch is placed close to the main patch (such as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-309" role="math" style="width: 5.348em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.808em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.81em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-310"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-311"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-312" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-313"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-314"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-315" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-316" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-317" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-318" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-319"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-320"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-321"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-322"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-323" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">h_{3}=1\ {\hbox{mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), a slight effect on the performance of the antenna is observed. Increasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-324" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-325"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-326"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-327" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-328"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-329"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-330" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">h_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> makes the antenna size larger, and thus, shifts down the operating band.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Effect of the height of the parasitic patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-331" role="math" style="width: 1.26em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.995em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001em 2.583em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-332"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-333"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.995em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.53em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-334" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.599em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-335"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-336"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-337" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.254em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">h_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> on the antenna performance. (a) Return loss. (b) AR. (c) Gain.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4d"><h3>D. Diameter of Feeding Probes <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-338" role="math" style="width: 0.574em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.522em; height: 0px; font-size: 112%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1000.5em 2.289em -999.98em); top: -2.128em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-339"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-340" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.133em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.055em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.934em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h3><p>The study shows that the diameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-341" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-342"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-343" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the feeding probe has a slight effect on impedance matching, AR, and gain. However, the very thin probe causes poor impedance matching and AR, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>. The long and thin feeding probes introduce a large inductance to degrade the impedance matching. Furthermore, the large inductance also disturbs the phase characteristic at the feeding point, and thus, degrades the AR performance. The feeding probes with a diameter of 2–3 mm are recommended in practical design.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Effect of the probe diameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-344" role="math" style="width: 0.665em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.532em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.53em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-345"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-346" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> on the antenna performance. (a) Return loss. (b) AR.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4e"><h3>E. Extension of the Open-Circuited Strip <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-347" role="math" style="width: 1.042em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.938em; height: 0px; font-size: 112%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1000.92em 2.445em -999.98em); top: -2.128em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-348"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-349"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.938em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.172em 1000.5em 4.159em -999.98em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-350" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.842em; left: 0.522em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-351"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-352"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-353" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.133em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.23em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.05em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">d_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h3><p>The open-circuited feed line configuration simplifies the antenna implementation and reduces the fabrication cost. However, the open-circuited termination will cause reflection on the feed line, and thus, affect the magnitudes and phase difference of the feeding currents at the four probes. The effect of the extension of the open-circuited strip is illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>. A severe effect on the AR has been observed. Optimal AR is achieved when the last probe is positioned at the edge of the strip line. Increasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-354" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.96em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-355"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-356"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-357" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-358"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-359"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-360" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">d_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> greatly degrades the AR. When <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-361" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.96em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-362"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-363"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-364" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-365"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-366"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-367" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">d_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> reaches 25 mm, the AR is larger than 3 dB over the entire frequency band.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806172/4806172-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Effect of the extension of the open-circuited strip <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-368" role="math" style="width: 1.194em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.929em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.93em 2.517em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-369"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-370"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.929em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute;
